Case of Fraudulent Claim of May 30th Compensation 127

Yu Qiaqing Sends a Letter Requesting Thorough Investigation

Lawyer Wu Urges Justice

The families of the martyrs of the May 30th Massacre in Shanghai stated that Li Ruiqing, Wang Zhaohua (i.e., Wang Daohua), and He Hanwen (i.e., He Shaoqing), employees of the small Shadujing Cotton Mill, instructed someone to impersonate Luo Wenlang, the family member of Luo Wenzhao, and colluded with Zhichengtai Tea House at No. 152 Maode Road, Xiaoshadu, to forge evidence to impersonate Luo Wenlang, the family member of Luo Wenzhao, and stamped and guaranteed to fraudulently claim 2,000 yuan in compensation from the association. They then instructed someone to impersonate Hu Changsheng, a representative of the association, to Luo Wenlang's residence, saying that Luo's compensation was only 500 yuan and that 260 yuan for travel expenses had to be deducted, leaving only 240 yuan for Luo. After the case was revealed, the association hired lawyer Wu Chengyu to sue Li, Wang, and He and Zhichengtai Tea House in the Special Zone Local Court. The court had already held a trial on the sixth day. Due to the lack of witnesses, the trial was adjourned. However, the fairy scene of this case is already very clear. Yesterday, Mr. Yu Qiaqing, chairman of the Board of Directors of the May 30th Cemetery, sent a special letter to Wu Chengyu, the acting lawyer of the families association, requesting him to advocate justice according to the law. The original letter said, "Dear Sir, Since the May 30th Massacre occurred, the families of the victims established a families association, and Hu Changsheng and Chen Fucai were publicly elected as representatives. This has long been reported to various government agencies. The association is supervised by the Board of Directors of the May 30th Cemetery. I am a member of the board and know that the representatives Hu Changsheng and Chen Fucai have been running around alone for five years, enduring hardships and never giving up. They are worthy of admiration. In January of this year, they received 150,000 yuan in compensation, and the method of distribution has been approved by the board of directors and passed by a majority of the families, and has been reported to the National Government. Because Li Ruiqing, Wang Zhaohua, and He Hanwen colluded with Zhichengtai Tea House to guarantee the impersonation of Luo Wenlang and fraudulently claimed 2,000 yuan in compensation from Luo Wenzhao, they later sent Luo Wenlang 240 yuan. However, this case concerns international reputation, social morality, and the reputation of the families association, as well as the personality of the two representatives Hu and Chen. It has been filed in the Special Zone Local Court according to law, requesting a thorough investigation. I believe that the two representatives Hu and Chen have always been fair, and when paying the compensation, they followed the instructions of the board of directors and issued it with a guarantee, and the procedures were complete. Please ask your lawyer to advocate human justice according to the law to clarify right and wrong and to warn against illegality.

Notorious Thief from Liyang Arrested in Shanghai 128

Detectives from the Liyang County Government reported to the French Concession Patrol Room the day before yesterday that the bandit Liu Deqing, also known as Pan Gonghui, colluded with bandits in Liyang County to commit major crimes in the county many times in the 17th year of the Republic of China. After the case was revealed, he fled to Shanghai and hid in a certain inn under his jurisdiction. They requested assistance in arresting him for investigation. The police chief approved the request and immediately ordered the detective to go with the patrolman to arrest Liu and bring him to the patrol room. Yesterday, the court was asked to investigate. First, the detectives reported the previous situation. When asked about Liu Deqing, he confessed that he had conspired to commit robbery. The Chinese and Western officials approved the transfer of the defendant to the detectives for investigation and trial.

Store Owner Accuses Department of Relief of Embezzlement 129

Xiang, now wants to transfer the store to Ma Jinwan, a native of Kunshan, who is in charge of relief. The day before yesterday, the two parties went to the Hongxiang Hotel on Avenyue Edward to negotiate. Lu took the opportunity to file a complaint with the Xinzha Patrol Room, accusing Ma of embezzling 2,218 taels of relief silver and more than 200 yuan since the 16th year of the Republic of China, and claiming that Ma was about to flee, requesting immediate arrest. The police chief sent detective Che Xuezeng to the hotel to arrest Ma. Yesterday, he was taken to the Special Zone Local Court. Judge Wu interrogated him. Lu stated the amount of embezzlement and theft of relief funds by the defendant. Ma denied that he had embezzled anything, saying that he only recorded the relief items and had never handled the funds. He hired a lawyer to argue that he was indeed lured and arrested by Lu's false accusations. Judge Wu then ordered Ma to pay 2,000 yuan bail and adjourned the trial for further questioning.

Wife Commits Suicide in Anger Over Husband's Affair 130

Ma Along, a local, is 28 years old and lives in a bungalow at No. 1322 Caomao Road, Hongkou. He is the head of the stonemasons in the Public Works Department. Eight years ago, he married Qiu, 27 years old, through a matchmaker. They have a daughter named Gendi, who is just eight years old. The relationship between the couple has been good in the past, but recently Ma has had an affair with a woman outside, causing him to often not return home. Sometimes when Qiu asked him about it, he would use social engagements as an excuse. Who knew that he had not returned home for four days recently? Qiu was shocked and feared that something unexpected had happened. She went to the bureau to visit, but Ma was not there. Ma's friend told her the truth. Qiu suddenly understood. The night before, Ma returned home after finishing his work. Qiu argued with him, and they had a quarrel. Because the secret had been leaked, Ma became angry and embarrassed and severely beat Qiu. At this point, Qiu was so painful that she did not want to live. Taking advantage of the fact that no one was prepared, she swallowed opium in an attempt to commit suicide. Before long, Ma realized what had happened and took her to Tongren Hospital by car. Fortunately, the treatment was early, and she was soon out of danger.

Pudong 131

Several Families Robbed in Xujialu Town

On the night of the eighth day (i.e., the day before yesterday), more than 20 robbers holding fast guns suddenly came to Xujialu Town, Chuansha North, and broke into the Hexing Cotton Ginning Field opened by Li Yunhai. They robbed about 1,000 yuan worth of silver dollars, clothing, and jewelry on the spot. At the same time, the Yuanxing Nanhua Store set up by Zhang Wenqing, the lace shop set up by Cai Rongxiang, and the family of Xia Changsheng were also robbed of clothing, jewelry, silver dollars, etc., worth about 1,000 yuan. They also tied up Zhang, the daughter-in-law of Xia Changsheng. When they left, they fired their guns as a demonstration and roared away. The merchants and residents of the town quickly reported to the Gu Town Public Security Bureau and telephoned the Sixth District and Donggou Public Security Bureau. They immediately led the police to search and arrest them, but they had gone like a yellow crane. At dawn, a suspect who looked like a worker carrying a power bucket was arrested and brought to the district. However, there was no evidence after interrogation. However, it was suspicious in the middle of the night. The division will rule on it according to law, it is said.

Angered by Someone Dismantling His Hustle, He Hanged Himself 132

Pan Adong, 38 years old, from Huzhou, lived at No. 17 Hengtong Lane, Hengtong Road, Zhabei. He used to be a shop clerk in a silk factory. He has been unemployed for a long time. His wife, Pan Zhu, is someone he met halfway. She is a hostess at the New New Company. In the afternoon of the day before yesterday, Pan Adong hanged himself at home behind people's backs. By the time his wife rescued him, it was too late to bring him back to life. A suicide note written in pencil by Pan was found on the table. The words were mostly nonsensical and full of typos. The words roughly said that Shao Jingui at No. 44 Changle Lane, Changan Road, scolded me twice. I really have no face to live. Shao Jingui also dismantled my hustle and took 20 yuan. He took 10 yuan on the 26th. There are still 10 yuan, and the agreed date has arrived, so I am determined to commit suicide, etc. His wife took the report to the Fourth District Police Station. Yesterday, he ordered Shen Xiaohe, the security guard of the 27th Bao 11th Tu, to report to the local court for investigation. Prosecutor Yang and the investigators arrived at the scene and found that it was indeed a suicide by hanging. The body was ordered to be collected by the family, and the investigation will be ordered, it is said.

Miss Ji Yin, of Yin Family, Proved to Have Died by Hanging 133

Miss Ji Yin, a young woman from Haizhou, residing at No. 21, Yude Lane, Dongchang Road, Pudong, had an argument with her husband, Ji Xiaoshunzi, over a food issue. This angered the husband and led to a conflict. Unexpectedly, Miss Yin became furious and hanged herself at home on the evening of the 7th, resulting in her death. The day before yesterday, Xie Along, the local security officer of the 24th District, reported the case to the local court, requesting an autopsy. However, it was too late in the day to proceed. Yesterday morning, Xu, the prosecutor, and Xue, the coroner, were appointed by the court to cross the river to conduct the examination. The corpse's internal organs were found to be decaying, and blood-like foam was gushing out of the mouth, confirming death by hanging. The husband, Ji Xiaoshunzi, was ordered to promptly arrange for the coffin and burial. If the deceased's maternal family had any grievances, they could go to the court for legal proceedings.

News of a Male Corpse Found Dead 134

Yesterday, an unidentified male corpse was found dead at the entrance of Wan Yu Street, Yanling Lane, Wangjia Wharf in the South City. He appeared to be in his twenties, wearing a worn-out Yuanbu cotton-padded robe and Yuanbu cotton trousers. He was a young man in distress, a stranger passing away in a foreign land. Lu Yongde, the local head of the 16th District, reported the case to the local court for an autopsy. After inspection by Prosecutor Yang and others, it was determined that he had died of illness. Photographs were taken, and the body was taken to the hall for collection and awaiting claim.

Further news: Rong Yonggen's adopted son, Rong Ziyuan, 21 years old, from Wuxi, had developed a smoking addiction, neglected his proper occupation, and was also rebellious. Ziyuan's situation worsened day by day, and he faced increasing hardship. Consequently, he repeatedly borrowed money from Su Zhu, a local woman residing at No. 27 Wan Yu Street, to spend. She became overwhelmed by this. Around 7 p.m. the night before, Ziyuan went to Su's house again to ask for a loan. She refused. Ziyuan then left the door. Suddenly, his addiction flared up, and he collapsed and died on the ground. Qian Dianjia, the guard of the 7th post in the area, heard about the incident, came to investigate, and took the woman, Rong Yonggen, and others to the first branch of the first district police station. Under preliminary interrogation by the station chief, the case involved human life, and Lu Yongde, the local head of the 16th District, was ordered to report for an autopsy. The autopsy confirmed that Rong Ziyuan had died of illness. The family was ordered to quickly prepare a coffin for burial. However, nearby residents said that the deceased, Rong Ziyuan, was from Wuxi. His biological father, Song, lived in Hangzhou. Due to a disagreement between his father and mother, they ended their marital relationship. His mother, Song, brought Ziyuan to Shanghai. Later, due to livelihood issues, she remarried Rong Yonggen. Ziyuan lived with his mother and was adopted under the Rong surname in name only. After being driven out, he often borrowed money from Su Zhu. The night before, he borrowed money from her again, but she refused. Ziyuan pleaded repeatedly, angering her. She immediately went outside and called the local police, who dragged Ziyuan out and told him to leave quickly. Ziyuan continued to beg, but the police angrily drove him away. Afterward, he collapsed on the ground. A crowd gathered to watch.

Losing Money Gambling Leads to a Life Lost 135

Yao Shifu Dies by Hanging

Yao Shifu, 37, from Taizhou, residing at No. 3327 Zhoujiazui Road, Hongkou, used to work as a waiter in the Tong Le Chun restaurant. Now unemployed, he occasionally worked as a substitute, earning a modest income and possessing over a hundred gold coins. The night before, he was invited by a friend to a gambling den. Initially, he made small bets, but unfortunately, he had bad luck and lost repeatedly. Later, he made larger bets, intending to fight to the death, but by midnight, he had lost all his money and left in a sorry state. He went to the Tong Le Chun to spend the night. Tossed and turned in bed, feeling extremely frustrated and angry. He hanged himself in the doorway that night. By dawn, people tried to rescue him, but it was too late. The restaurant owner reported the case to the Jiaxing Road police station, and police officer No. 154 went to investigate. The body was taken to the morgue for an autopsy.

Woman Commits Suicide by Swallowing Opium 136

Shi Renxue, a Ningbo native residing in Shangxian Lane, Zhujia Wooden Bridge, Hongkou, earns a meager income of only six and a half yuan, leading to a difficult life. His wife, Wu, often argued with him over this. The afternoon before yesterday, the couple had another quarrel. Wu, in anger, swallowed opium. The poisoning was severe, and she was taken to Tongren Hospital. She died after 4 o'clock. The hospital reported the case to the police station.

The police officer ordered the body to be transported to the Feifeilun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor appointed by the Special District Court, arrived at the morgue and examined the body. He sat in the official position and questioned the husband, Shi Renxue. He announced that the autopsy confirmed that Shi Wu had died from taking opium and ordered her husband to claim the body for burial.

Careless Cause of the Wuzhou Solid Foundation Factory Accident 137

At 3 p.m. yesterday, the bottom of the furnace in the smelly water distillation room of the Wuzhou Solid Foundation Factory in Xujiahui collapsed, causing flames to spill out. Fortunately, the location was surrounded by open space. Fire trucks and factory workers worked hard to put out the fire, extinguishing it in half an hour. Only one iron shed was destroyed, and the fire did not spread elsewhere, nor were any people injured. It is said that the distillation room was not insured, so the losses were limited.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated that the sky in the northern and Yangtze River basins was cloudy, with occasional fog. There was rain in the Taiwan Strait. The wind direction above the Yellow Sea and East China Sea was uncertain. The weather in central Japan was severe due to a low-pressure system moving northeast. Yesterday, in the 24 hours before 3 p.m., the highest temperature in Shanghai was 86.0 degrees, and the lowest was 64.4 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 73.8 degrees, and the lowest was 54.7 degrees.

Amendment to the Judicial Yuan Regulations 165

Supervision of National University Law Departments Article 2

The Ministry of Education, upon the order of the Executive Yuan, hereby announces that the National Government has revised and promulgated Article 2 of the Regulations of the Judicial Yuan on Supervising National University Law Departments and specially orders subordinate provincial and municipal education administrative agencies to take note of it. The original text of Article 2 of the Regulations of the Judicial Yuan on Supervising National University Law Departments revised and promulgated by the National Government is recorded below: (Article 2) The law departments of national universities shall take the following subjects as required courses: (1) The Three Principles of the People; (2) Constitution; (3) Civil Law and Commercial Law; (4) Criminal Law; (5) Civil Procedure Law; (6) Criminal Procedure Law; (7) Court Organization Law; (8) Administrative Law; (9) Private International Law; (10) Public International Law; (11) Political Science; (12) Economics; (13) Sociology; (14) Labor Law. The teaching time of the aforementioned subjects shall account for two-thirds or more of the total teaching time in the law department.

Amendment to the Regulations 166

of the Judicial Yuan on Licensing the Establishment of Private Law and Political Science Schools

The National Government promulgated the amended Regulations of the Judicial Yuan on Licensing the Establishment of Private Law and Political Science Schools, comprising seven articles, as follows: Article 1: The following private schools must be licensed by the Judicial Yuan: (1) Law schools within universities; (2) Independent law schools; (3) Independent colleges with law or political science departments. Article 2: In addition to the approval for establishment and commencement of operations by the Ministry of Education, the private schools listed in the preceding article shall also submit documents to the Judicial Yuan for review through the Ministry of Education when applying for a license. The documents shall be submitted by the school board and shall include: (1) Proof of registration approved by the Ministry of Education; (2) The proposed curriculum for the law or political science department; (3) Resumes of the faculty members of the law or political science department; (4) Equipment and plan books for the law or political science department. Article 3: If the Judicial Yuan deems that the facilities of the private school applying for a license under the preceding article are incomplete, it may order the school to improve its facilities within a reasonable period. Article 4: After the establishment of a private school listed in Article 1 of these Regulations is licensed by the Judicial Yuan, the Judicial Yuan shall notify the Ministry of Education and inform the Examination Yuan for record and publish it in the Government Gazette. Article 5: If the performance of a school established under the license of these Regulations is poor, the Judicial Yuan may order it to improve or revoke its license. In addition to notifying the Ministry of Education of the revocation of the license under the preceding paragraph, it shall inform the Examination Yuan for record and publish it in the Government Gazette. Article 6: Any reorganization or change in the law school or law department of a school established under the license of these Regulations shall be submitted to the Judicial Yuan through the Ministry of Education for approval. The abolition of the law school or law department under the preceding paragraph shall be submitted to the Judicial Yuan through the Ministry of Education for record. Article 7: These Regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. Before the implementation of these Regulations, private universities or independent colleges registered with the Ministry of Education or the former University Council shall apply for a license retroactively, and the procedures shall be determined separately by the Judicial Yuan.

Local News

Feihong and Four Other Municipal Schools 167

in the Concessions Request the Recovery of Educational Rights in the Concessions

Letter to the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department

Chen Dezheng, the Director of the Shanghai Special Municipality Education Bureau, solemnly issued a declaration on the 4th of this month to recover educational rights in the concessions, which has been recorded in previous newspapers. Yesterday, the principals of the municipal Feihong and four other schools in the concession area also wrote to the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department, stating the urgency of reorganizing Chinese education in the concessions and the necessity of recovering educational rights. The following is recorded: To Mr. Yuan Ludeng, Mr. Yu Qiaqing, Mr. Xu Xinzhi, Mr. Bei Songsun, and Mr. Liu Hongsheng, the Chinese Directors of the Public Works Department, esteemed sirs: We sincerely congratulate you on being elected as Chinese Directors of the Public Works Department of the concessions, as you are expected by the public. We are even more admirable for your enthusiasm and perseverance in implementing the proposal of increasing the number of Chinese Directors for taxpayers. At the beginning of your assumption of office, it is a great fortune that the Municipal Education Bureau has proposed to recover educational rights in the concessions. With your wisdom, you are well aware of the current state of education in the concessions. With your ability, you will certainly promote the realization of the Municipal Education Bureau's proposal to recover educational rights in the concessions. Our schools are all located in the concessions and are particularly hopeful for the realization of this proposal. Therefore, we would like to offer a few humble suggestions and hope that you will consider them. The Chinese education managed by the Public Works Department of the concessions has already been suffered by the Chinese children in our concessions. Given the large amount of rent paid by the Chinese, the Chinese education expenditure of the Public Works Department accounts for less than two percent of its total income, which is not comparable to the 20% of the municipal government's education expenditure, nor is it comparable to the 30% of the education expenditure of foreign cities. Given the size of the concession area and the large number of Chinese children, the number of Chinese children's schools established by the Public Works Department is less than ten, and most of their contents do not conform to the educational purposes of our country. Every Chinese in the concessions has children, and everyone wants their children to receive a good education from an early age. Today, the enrollment of Chinese children in the concessions has become a major problem. What could be worse? Our schools are located in the concessions and have always regarded Chinese education in the concessions as our own responsibility. However, the number of Chinese children in the concessions is so large that these four schools are just a drop in the bucket. Although we have been trying our best to expand over the years, every time school starts, the number of applicants to our schools exceeds the fixed enrollment quota by tenfold, and we cannot accommodate them as much as we would like. Is this not a pity? Now, for the sake of the Chinese Directors in the concessions, it is urgent to reorganize Chinese schools in the concessions and seek expansion. The Chinese education expenditure of the Public Works Department must be increased to at least 20% of its total income. The Chinese education administration in the concessions must be unified and directly administered by the Municipal Education Bureau. The Chinese children's schools already run by the Public Works Department should be handed over to the Education Bureau for reception and rectification, and the Education Bureau should plan to set up more municipal schools in the concessions. As for the problems of private schools and substandard private schools in the concessions, they can be solved. Thinking of the welfare of the Chinese in the concessions, we rely on you to think about the Chinese children in the concessions and urge the Public Works Department to realize this as soon as possible. We are extremely grateful. We have taken the liberty to state our views and await your instructions. We wish you all the best. Tang Tiantao, Principal of Shanghai Special Municipal Feihong Primary School; Wang Dingcheng, Principal of Bide Primary School; Zhou Darong, Principal of Shuji Primary School; Qian Xuanqing, Principal of He'an Primary School, May 9th.

Ye Gongchuo 168

Gave an Academic Lecture at Jinan University Yesterday

Hoping that Modern Writers of Ci Can Create a New Realm

Beyond the Scenery and Integrate Understanding and Set People to Musical Tunes

Mr. Ye Gongchuo lectured at Jinan University yesterday at the invitation of Mr. Chen Zhu, the head of the Department of Chinese Language and Literature. First, Vice President Hong Ji introduced him, and then Mr. Ye took the stage to speak. The topic of the lecture was "Photography of Qing Dynasty Ci Studies." Mr. Ye used scientific methods to sort out and historical perspectives to compare and evaluate the Ci writers of the Qing Dynasty. He listed them in tables, horizontally dividing them by region. Jiangsu and Zhejiang were the most prosperous. Jiangsu produced as many as 2,009 Ci writers in the Qing Dynasty, and Zhejiang produced 1,248. Anhui, Guangdong, Fujian, Jiangxi, and Hunan were next, and Gansu and Mongolia were the least, with three each. Chahar, Suiyuan, Rehe, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Xinjiang had none. A total of 4,850 people were counted, with 4,233 having registered residences. However, there were still omissions, and the total could reach about 6,000 people. Vertically, the Shunzhi period inherited the remaining style of the late Ming Dynasty, with 188 people. The Qianlong period had 362 people, and the Jiaqing period had 328 people, all considered prosperous. The Daoguang period had the most, reaching 440 people, likely influenced by the prevalence of the Changzhou Ci school. The above is from a quantitative observation. The large number of Ci writers in the Qing Dynasty can be imagined. From a qualitative perspective, the Song Dynasty was the most prosperous for Ci writers, and Ci studies were also extremely complete. The Yuan Dynasty was second, but Song people regarded Ci as mere recreational writing after tea and wine, and its style was not very noble. The Yuan Dynasty was second, and the Ming Dynasty regarded it as a low-grade product of weaving and enchanting beauty. In the Qing Dynasty, Zhejiang took the lead, and Zhu Yizun and others emerged, reforming the bad habits of the Ming Dynasty. After the Jiaqing period, the Changzhou school emerged, with Zhang Huiyan and Zhou Ji at the forefront, focusing on broad-mindedness and artistic conception, and the spirit of Ci was greatly enhanced. The Daoguang, Xianfeng, Tongzhi, Guangxu, and Xuantong periods were influenced by it. The Guipai school followed, and Wang Pengyun and Kuang Zhouyi of the Guangxu period used the Changzhou school as a foundation, gradually evolving and adding their unique views, and the atmosphere changed again. However, what the three schools agreed on without prior consultation was to elevate the status of Ci and regard it as a noble literature. Therefore, its advantage lies in its ability to respect the foundation, and the second is strict adherence to the rules. Ci was originally valued for its ability to be sung with music. Later generations lost the musical rhythm, and the Ci of the Southern Song, Yuan, and Ming Dynasties did not conform to the rhythm. There were also many Ci that did not conform to the rhythm in the early Qing Dynasty during the Shunzhi and Kangxi periods. Since Wan Shida of the Shunzhi and Yongzheng periods fixed the Ci rhythm, and Ge Zai of the Jiaqing and Xianfeng periods fixed the 词谱 (cípǔ), the books of the two became the norms for Ci writing by various families in later generations. After the Xianfeng period, the rhythm was even stricter, and the five sounds of yin and yang were analyzed clearly. Various academic studies in the Qing Dynasty surpassed the previous dynasties, and this was not limited to Ci studies. However, Ci was particularly prominent. Dong Shi said that poetry, Ci, and song were originally the same but diverged. The poetry and song of the Qing Dynasty generally could not surpass the Ming Dynasty, but the efforts made by the Ci writers were unique. In the history of Chinese literature, whether viewed horizontally or vertically, it occupies an important position. Therefore, we can draw a conclusion: the Ci of the Qing Dynasty surpassed the Ming Dynasty and directly inherited the Song and Yuan Dynasties. Predecessors in Ci writing focused on two points: emotion and scenery, or scenery with emotion, or generating emotion based on the scenery, or integrating emotion and scenery. However, according to my personal opinion, in the future, if Ci studies want to evolve and create a new realm, understanding can be added in addition to emotion and scenery. This "understanding" may not have been mentioned by predecessors. The integration of emotion, scenery, and understanding can create a new realm through imagination, which can surpass the predecessors. This may be possible. Filling in Ci without restraint does not conform to the rhyme, but conforming to the rhyme does not mean it can be set to music. The original sources of rhyme are mostly impossible to verify, so one can only fill in according to the old tunes. However, the tunes of Ci were also created by predecessors. Why can't we create new tunes? If we can examine their origins, we can create from our own musical ideas. We can even compose music for them. Zhu Yizun of the late Ming Dynasty was the first step in organizing the efforts. We can do this kind of change after the prosperity of Qing Dynasty Ci. I hope that those who aspire to write Ci will trace back to the source and work hard to create new Ci," he said. The lecture lasted about an hour and a half and was very engaging. Finally, Mr. Chen Zhu expressed his gratitude on behalf of the department.

Free Talk

Pay with a Laugh · Guest ·

Doctor A: I see you often take people for drives, which is a bit of an indulgence.

Doctor B: Yes, but I think it's good for their health, so I make a point of pleasing them.

Doctor A: My hospital would never do such a thing. Only an idiot like you would do such an idiotic thing.

Doctor B: True. I see patients from your hospital often going for drives, with bands and retinues.

Woman A: The Wang family next door has lost their fourth child.

Woman B: So fast. What was the illness?

Woman A: A sudden attack. The Wang family is so lucky. All four children died of sudden illnesses. They didn't even have time to call a doctor, saving them a fortune in medical fees.

Woman A: My husband used to smoke twenty or thirty rolled cigarettes every day before we got married, but for the past five years, he hasn't smoked a single one.

Woman B: That's good. It takes harsh methods and a hard heart to break a long-standing habit like that.

Woman A: I have both in abundance, which is why he was able to quit.

Daughter: My brother lost his temper upstairs and beat me up.

Mother: What for?

Daughter: I only opened a can of sardine fish with his shaving razor.

After Mr. Ma Xiangbo's Ninetieth Birthday 171

Lu Jingqing

On the fourth of this month, contemporary celebrities gathered at Aurora University to celebrate the ninetieth birthday of Mr. Ma Xiangbo. The Aurora University Alumni Association, led by Wei Tingrong, Zhu Yanzhi, He Shangping, and myself, served as hosts, so I have more detailed information. I will record it as follows.

Calligraphy and Birthday Couplets: Cai Zimin wrote couplets for Ms. Ge Chenghui, a former student of the Patriotic Girls' School, and Ms. Zhou Jun (i.e., Cai's wife): "Wonderful metaphors are like Mount Cen, a mustard seed; learning increases daily, a great catalpa tree for a thousand autumns." Yu Youren wrote couplets on behalf of Fudan University: "He is a paragon of virtue in this era, a Fusheng in the scientific community." Yang Xingfo's couplet was: "The four seas share a realm of benevolence and longevity, the teacher laughs heartily over eight thousand fields." Wang Jingqi collected couplets from the Book of Changes: "Sharpening virtue and talent, serving as assistants to the country; cultivating the Way and nurturing longevity, extending the ruler's years." Xu Jilong, a hermit of Mount Huang, wrote birthday poems, four large scrolls in total, full of emotional sighs and melancholy, with flamboyant brushstrokes. Zhang Taiyan's calligraphy couplets were also ancient, simple, and neat. Zhang Qi, a six-year-old boy (the son of Mr. Taiyan), wrote the birthday plaque "Longevity comparable to Golden Jiao (Island)," which had quite a structure and was praised as a genius. Guan Jin, an old man, painted a pine and Ganoderma lucidum longevity painting, which was naturally extraordinary from an old master (presented by Mr. Wu Tegong and others from this museum). Ms. Yang Xuejiu's pine-age stone longevity painting was elegant, vigorous, and had the style of a White Dragon Mountain person.

Daily Life and Health Care: As I have been living with Mr. Xiang for many years, I know him quite well. Mr. Xiang is a devout Catholic. Every morning at around five o'clock, he must go up and down three floors to attend Mass in the church, even in wind and rain. In the cold winter, when it is still dark, he goes downstairs with a cane. At other times, like Yang Tieya in his later years, he does not go downstairs. He usually does not eat rice or vegetables, but mainly consumes chicken juice, beef juice, chicken eggs, and milk. He is diligent in bathing and sleeps for one or two hours in the afternoon, which is his routine. During the day, he always has a book in his hand and rarely exercises, which is completely different from the hygiene of Wu Zhiyong and Okuma Shigenobu. He has read many Buddhist scriptures and has unique insights. Mr. Xiang and Yang Renshan also worked together on Sakura Island in his early years. On that day, Cai Yuanpei, Yu Youren, and Yang Xingfo all gave speeches, which were full of wit. The birthday honoree, known for his wonderful language, also gave a very long speech, which I will record separately.

The Number One Poet in Zheng Sukan's Eyes · He · Tian · Jian ·

A scholar born in this age who wants to be valued by his ancient literature, although he may not suffer the humiliation of wearing a 章甫 (zhāngfǔ, a type of hat) in Yue (a metaphor for misplaced talent), it is inevitable that he will be blind and difficult to see himself. Fortunately, even in the dark and stormy weather, the rooster crows incessantly. There are still experienced adults. Yesterday, Wu Chang told me about Mr. Zheng Sukan's encounter with a poet, which is worth recording. One day, a man in his fifties or older visited Mr. Zheng. After a brief exchange of pleasantries, he said solemnly and sincerely, "You are a literary giant of our time. I do not want to seek fame at the Dragon Gate. I am going to decide my progress and retreat on your guidance. Are you interested?" Zheng asked about the matter. He said, "I have been studying poetry for nearly thirty years, and I have created countless works, but I am walking blindly and do not know where I am going. Now I want to get a word from you to determine my next step." Zheng felt sorry for his intention and immediately asked to read his poems. The man was delighted and promised to present them for review on a certain day. Zheng flipped through his poems, one or two volumes, and exclaimed, "This is the number one poet of our time. He is my teacher!" The man looked around hesitantly, overwhelmed by the honor. The next day, Zheng told others about this, and they all wanted to read his poems and see his demeanor. Alas! After more than fifty years of cultivation, he gained fame overnight with a word from Mr. Zheng. Such a person also knows how to guard himself and see himself. From the incident, we can infer that his poems are clear and orderly. Then, the world is so big, how can we be complacent?

The Grand Occasion of the Buddha's Birthday · Zhou · Cai · Liang · 172

Yesterday (the eighth day of the fourth lunar month) was the birthday of the Buddha, Sakyamuni. Jing'an Temple in West Shanghai had its usual incense market. On this day, the sky was clear and the air was fresh, and the gentle breeze was pleasant. Men and women who were enjoying the spring gathered there. Jing'an Temple Road, from morning to dusk, was packed with people, like the mountain path of Shanyin. The temple was crowded, the incense was thick, and the excitement was unprecedented in recent years. I am a student at Zhengfeng, which is nearby. I heard and saw many interesting things, so I will briefly record one or two of them based on what I observed.

Buddha Lao Serves as Matchmaker: In the morning, I happened to be playing in the temple and met a couple dressed in fancy clothes, whispering sweet words and walking arm in arm into the inner hall. They both bowed down in front of the altar very respectfully, and seemed to be praying: "We are in love and wish to be companions forever. I hope that the Buddha will be merciful and help us become husband and wife as soon as possible." The rest of the words were too soft to hear, which was a pity. At that time, the onlookers all looked at them, not knowing what was happening. I thought that the couple's love must have reached its peak, so they were unrestrained and unashamed. It can be said that they are thinking too much by using Buddha Lao as a matchmaker.

Women's Army Fighting: Most of the incense and candle stalls at the temple gate were set up by women. Although the business was good, the competition was fierce. From time to time, several women from the countryside would choose things from Stall A for a long time, but eventually, they did not succeed due to the high price. They then bought from Stall B, and the woman from Stall A started a war. At first, it was just arguing, and then they started fighting. They punched and kicked each other. Later, the onlookers persuaded them to stop, but both sides had already been beaten badly.

Foreigners Being Fooled: The temporary markets set up on the roads near the temple mostly sold household goods of various colors. Since the number of visitors was large this time, each store made three times its profit. Some unscrupulous people started to do business unscrupulously. I saw a foreigner in a certain store buying about ten paper suitcases and happily bundling them up and leaving. I was surprised and asked the owner of the store about the price. The owner smiled and said, "I make the most profit and have the best business selling this thing (paper is easy to break). Now he bought my goods at twice the price and still thinks they are cheap. Aren't foreigners foolish?" I sighed and said, "The reason why our country's commerce is not prosperous is all because of the despicable behavior of those people. They only know the immediate benefits and do not care about the long-term harm, and their failure is appropriate.

Yizheng's Three-Day Diary (1) - A Complete Record by Xie Fensheng, Leader of the National Hiking Group 173

April 16th, 9:30 AM. Together with my comrades, we departed from Liuhe County, exiting through the east gate. We set off towards Yizheng County. That day, due to the recent rains, the roads were muddy. One could not help but sigh, "It's impossible to walk!" However, my comrades did not lose heart because of this. One step, one stumble, we still strived to move forward. At 11:35 AM, we arrived at Hengliangdian. We entered a village shop for lunch. Unfortunately, the area had suffered repeated poor harvests in the autumn, and the price of rice was high. The restaurant could not cook enough rice to satisfy the guests. I had to buy noodles and cook them myself to fill my stomach. At 12:20 PM, after a short rest, we resumed our journey towards Chenbanqiao. That day, the scorching sun beat down on our backs, and sweat soaked through our clothes. The sweat and mud under our feet were like paste, making it impossible to walk quickly. A distance of twenty *li* took us three hours. One can imagine how difficult the road was. We rested for about thirty minutes there, then continued forward. By the time we crossed Xupu Bridge, the setting sun had already disappeared, and the stars filled the sky. It was less than four *li* from the county seat, but it was already late (8:20 PM), and there were many forks in the road, making us unsure of which way to go. Helplessly, we retreated to Xupu Bridge. (Xupu Bridge is named for the place where Wu Zixu crossed the river.) The area is an important road on the western route of Yizheng. The county government had a police detachment stationed there with strict security. At that time, I explained everything to the soldiers of the detachment and presented official documents and passports to prove our identity. I requested to borrow a branch to perch on, intending to enter the city at dawn. However, there were only three or five rustic shops and a dozen thatched huts, with no place to stay. We were in a dilemma, and could only exclaim "Alas!" Fortunately, someone like a squad leader in the detachment said to me, "Gentlemen, you have worked hard to get here. We should try to help you, but the place is small and there are few houses, so we cannot accommodate all of you. We could make room for one or two, but we are helpless to assist your group of seven. However, I can send two soldiers to lead and escort you into the city." We were delighted and expressed our gratitude, following closely behind the leaders. Fortunately, we had electric torches, so we were not walking on a completely dark path, unable to distinguish between high and low ground. It was 10:00 PM when we finally reached the west gate. The leaders knocked on the gate and sent us in, lodging us at the Zhenzhou Inn. The innkeeper mistook us for soldiers and refused us, saying the inn was full. After I explained, he happily cleared a room for us. We ate a hearty meal and then went to bed. That day, we traveled seventy *li*. The pedometer recorded 71,654 steps, a new record for us since we set out.

Religious Bias and Sexual Frustration - Liuzhi 174

The Reason for the Assassination of the Inventor of the Art of Resurrection - Reading Mr. Huang Yingdai's "Talking About the Art of Resurrection" in the *Riben Tan* on the 28th, it briefly stated that Professor Miroski of the Central Asian University used scientific methods to bring monkeys back from the dead. He planned to apply this to humans in the hope of realizing the ideal of eternal life. Unexpectedly, he himself was suddenly assassinated, and his wife was suspected. I felt that he had not mentioned the reason for Mr. Miroski's assassination and why his wife was suspected of killing her husband. Presuming on my lack of talent, I dare to follow up like a dog's tail extending a sable coat. According to reports, Central Asia has always been known to the world for its isolation. The people are stuck in their ways and unchanging. Their customs and systems have remained almost the same for thousands of years. Although there is a new communist ideology and the modern spirit of the East permeating it, the religious color is still very strong. The news of Mr. Miroski's resurrection experiments aroused the anger of religious fanatics, who believed that only God is the omnipotent master. God wills that humans and monkeys die, and Mr. Miroski dared to advocate heretical arts in an attempt to defy this. If Mr. Miroski did not die, God would be in danger. Therefore, Mr. Miroski received various anonymous threats before his death and did not dare to take a step without armed protection. Mr. Miroski was highly respected and had never harbored grudges against anyone. Now that he has unfortunately been killed, the reason should not be other than this. Mrs. Miroski is a devout Catholic. She had some reservations about Mr. Miroski's experiments. Mr. Miroski had a secret diary that fell into the hands of others after his death. It contained suspicions that the anonymous threats were made by his wife. Moreover, the gun that killed Mr. Miroski was next to his body, and there were many fingerprints on it, many of which matched his wife's fingerprints. Therefore, her suspicion in this case is very significant. However, even if Mr. Miroski was killed by his wife, it is still questionable whether the motive was religious bias. Because a draft of a letter from Mr. Miroski to his relatives was found afterward, saying that he was so focused on his experiments that he forgot his marital responsibilities and had become an unfeeling husband. Then, Mrs. Miroski already felt great sexual frustration. This is also enough to trigger the murder.

Short News: *Chunshui Wei Bo*, published by Shanghai's Rose Bookstore, is the latest published social romance novel. Since the bookstore commissioned Xuzhou's World Bookstore to sell it on consignment, sales have been very strong. Mr. Liu Jingfu, Commander-in-Chief of the Second Army Corps of the National Revolutionary Army, also brought four attendants with him on the 25th of the month to purchase and read this book, and praised it. (Autumn Pestle, sent from Xuzhou)

Warmth in the Heart (1) (8) (9) - Bao Tianxiao 175

Chapter Ten: Red Flames Rise to the Sky, Goulan Praises the Filial Daughter, Red Carpet on the Ground, Impromptu Meeting with Famous Actors

Today, this bridegroom, Liu Yinbo, has always been a very generous and lively person. It is his own wedding celebration, so he is very happy. After the banquet was set up, several groomsmen had already invited the guests to take their seats. The bridegroom himself came out to toast everyone, and everyone invited him to sit down at their tables, saying, "You've worked very hard today, take a rest." But he couldn't sit still. He ran around, and then shouted, "Why don't you call a *ju*? Calling a *ju* will make it more lively, and you can also invite them to listen to the opera!" Everyone said, "Calling a *ju* is good, but the place is too far away, it's a bit inconvenient." Liu Yinbo said, "There's nothing inconvenient. We'll use carriages to pick them up." It turned out that at this time in Shanghai, cars were not yet very popular. Liu Yinbo had hired ten carriages to bring the many ladies and young ladies to the wedding banquet, so he said, "Quickly write out the *ju* tickets, and I'll tell the coachmen to pick them up one by one. With ten carriages here, three people can sit in one carriage, so you can call thirty *ju*! Moreover, after picking up one batch, you can turn around. The more you call, the more lively it will be." Everyone said, "Well, the Wei Chun Garden doesn't have *ju* tickets. Just grab some pieces of paper." At this time, the owner of the garden happened to be present and said, "No need, no need. I have them here. Tell them to go get them." He then called a tea boy named Ah Quan and said, "Go to the old foreign-style house and bring the guest tickets and *ju* tickets." It turned out that this Ankai residence was newly built, called the "new foreign-style house." There was also a foreign-style house to the north that was built earlier, called the "old foreign-style house." People often borrowed this place to host banquets, so they had all the guest tickets and *ju* tickets prepared there, just in case they were needed. After Ah Quan brought the *ju* tickets, Liu Yinbo even more happily told his brother, Xing Shu, to greet everyone at each table. Some people always called a *ju*, and some people never called a *ju*. He had them all written down, who called whom, and they could be divided by location and distributed in large quantities. Although the North Lane of Shanghai is all in one place, between Fuzhou Road and Zhejiang Road, it is still necessary to arrange them a little before handing them to the coachmen. Which *ju* would be picked up by which carriage? Because they were all on the same route. Counting the *ju* tickets, there were more than twenty. If all of them were picked up, these ten carriages would not be enough! Because in addition to the *ju* herself, there was also a follower. Didn't this already double the number of people? And some of them sang outside the hall, so they had to turn around and pick them up again. After dealing with this for half an hour, all ten carriages set off.

New Cocoons Appear in Jinhua and Lanxi 185

Affected by the weather, harvests are at most 60%.

The silkworm season in Jinhua and Lanxi, Zhejiang Province, is the earliest. Due to unrest in Youbu and other areas, fewer silkworms were raised. The weather turned cold after the mulberry leaves sprouted, delaying development. After the third molt, the weather became suddenly cold and hot, with continuous rain, making silkworm rearing difficult for farmers. During the peak of the fourth molt, the weather remained cold and rainy, causing widespread silkworm diseases and losses. Early silkworms have already spun cocoons, but the quality is poor. The cocoon market opens today, with low expected prices. It is estimated that this year's new cocoons in Jinhua and other counties will be at most 60% of a normal year.

Zhejiang Cocoons Subject to 10% Security Levy 186

The Zhejiang Provincial Government, in light of the unrest in various counties and the imminent arrival of new cocoons on the market, is concerned about silk and cocoon merchants carrying funds to purchase cocoons in various counties. It is imperative to increase military and police patrols to provide protection. The Security Department has now assigned military and police forces to maintain order in sections, with the total force exceeding previous years by more than 10%. The required funds are substantial. The Provincial Government's Political Affairs Committee has resolved to levy a 10% security donation on the dry-land tax to provide subsidies, with a term of one year. This has been announced and is being implemented.

Poor European Sales of Local Green Tea 187

Since local green tea from native estates came onto the market in this port, transactions have been very sparse for days. Tea firms have put out new samples of local "Zhenmei", already over 20 characters, totaling over one thousand chests. In the last few days, only Jardine Matheson and Ewo have purchased 109 chests, with selling prices from 76 to 107 taels. The poor sales to Europe can be seen. In addition, anti-British protests are occurring in India, and the Bombay market, which sells a lot of green tea, is particularly intense. Therefore, foreign tea merchants are tending to take a wait-and-see approach, and the market outlook is quite pessimistic.

US Bans Import of Colored Chinese Tea 188

The Shanghai-based British firm Jardine Matheson shipped various types of Lu Zhuang Ping Shui green tea to New York last year. After testing by the US government, it was found to contain white impurities and was banned from import, resulting in significant losses. They have already informed the Tea Guild and notified tea merchants in all regions that this year's green tea sold to the US should not contain any white color to avoid detection by the US government and a ban on import.

Rice Market in He Xia Continues to Stabilize 189

This is because japonica rice from Su and Ci is being shipped back to the mainland. The source of supply will become increasingly scarce in the future. Although sales in this street are taking a wait-and-see approach due to the arrival of foreign rice, demand for medium and high-quality goods is still active, making it difficult for the market to fall further. For the time being, the market may tend to fluctuate without surprises. Supplies of thin-husk rice are scarce and prices remain stable. Buying interest is weak, and the market lacks prosperity. Transactions of Yang Du Jian rice are slightly active. Merchants are unwilling to sell at a lower price, and the market appears stable. The price of white Yuan rice is high and firm. Yesterday's foreign rice market was slightly more active because, in addition to purchases by merchants and retailers in this street, merchants from Jiangxi Province were also buying in the market. Market sentiment was good. However, current rice inventories are sufficient, and several new ships have arrived, resulting in supply exceeding demand. It is ultimately difficult for prices to be supported. Therefore, the prices of medium-grade goods have all fallen by about a cent. High-quality goods such as Annam japonica rice saw no transactions, but sellers' intentions remained firm. The market may temporarily stabilize. 2,000 bags of Saigon No. 1 were sold for 15 yuan and 3 jiao 2 fen. Also, 1,000 bags of No. 2 for 14 yuan and 6 jiao 5 fen. 2,000 bags of "Da Jiao" for 14 yuan and 4 jiao 5 fen. 4,000 bags of "Xiao Jiao" for 14 yuan and 6 jiao 3 fen. Also, 4,000 bags of goods at 20 Jiaolu for 14 yuan and 4 jiao.

Piece Goods Market Stagnant 191

Piece goods trading has been quiet in recent days due to the off-season. Whether it's local merchants or out-of-town merchants, business is quite slow, so the market is even more lifeless. Except for the Yuan Yang yarn and white crepe, which are in short supply and showing strength, everything else is weak. The Changbanqiao straight tribute flannel, which was once out of stock, has arrived in 50 pieces and will be available for shipment next Tuesday. The price is set at 2 mace 8 fen less commission. There have been slight transactions in this street. There is no definite date for the arrival of the Qiu Xi Bi Ji. Shile Bird fine cloth had previously risen due to Tianjin merchants' purchases, but has now fallen back to 7 taels and 7 mace 5 fen. Blue striped Satin, printed cloth, and crepe remain very weak. The decline in civilized satin is even faster. Yesterday, both "Foreign Beauty" and "Yang Guifei" sold for 1 mace 5 fen 5 li, and "Yun Tongzi" at 1 mace 5 fen, willing to sell them off, showing a downward trend. The reason is that local products are gradually increasing, selling for only 1 mace 4 fen 5 li, coupled with sluggish sales. Yesterday, Changjiang merchants made slight transactions in Western goods blue striped cotton fabric. Jinlong Tian Tong Shan was 3 mace 8 fen 5 li, and Ewo's Women's Army was 3 mace 2 fen 5 li. Northern merchants bought more than 30 pieces of jacquard foreign yarn, and the prices were all around 3 mace 7 fen.

Sugar Market Tai Che Sugar Falls 2 Mace 192

Coarse granulated white sugar continues to decline... Minghua Factory to start operations tomorrow

Yesterday's telegram from the sugar market production area: The current price of Cuban sugar is still 1.50, and the price of New York May futures sugar is 1.41, compared to the previous telegram, there has been no rise or fall. September is 1.55, December is 1.64, March of next year is 1.72, compared to the previous one, only December fell by 2 fen, and September and March each recovered 2 fen. The current price of Java sugar is 9.50, a decrease of 25.67. June-July is 9.75, also a decrease of 125. The Shanghai Sugar Merchant Association's market for Dutch sugar No. 24 coarse granulated white, is facing sluggish sales due to abundant current inventory, and falling prices in foreign markets. Even if goods were offered for immediate shipment, Tianxiang Yanghang offered a price of 6 yuan 8 jiao new rules, but there was no interest, and the market became even weaker. Goods were rushed to be sold, and prices were trending downward. Yesterday's market price was 7 taels, but few hands were willing to buy. The market's weakness and the downward trend of prices has not yet stopped. Finely ground granulated white sugar was 7 taels 07 fen 5 li, and No. 20 medium granulated white sugar was 6 taels 9 mace, but transactions were also few. The import and export of Japanese sugar has slowed down. The Minghua Factory will start refining tomorrow, and the product should be delivered on the 13th, so the market has also turned flat. ET mark was 7 taels 6 mace, YP mark was 7 taels 8 mace, but transactions were also quiet. Tai Gu Che sugar has been out of the market for a long time, but suddenly fell 2 mace yesterday. HX mark was 7 taels 8 mace, top-grade B mark was 8 taels 1 mace 5 fen, BA mark five-temperature sugar was 10 taels 03 mace, CC mark Che ice sugar was 11 taels 5 mace, but demand was still silent, and the market was still weak.

Non-Ferrous Metals: Over 60 Tons of Coarse Lead Wire Fixed 193

Coarse lead wire, such as #12 and #14, has been actively traded in this port recently. There is a general shortage of goods on the market, and prices are steadily increasing. The current price has risen to 9 taels. The highest estimated price for #12 is 9 taels 5 mace, and #14 is 9 taels 6 mace. It is reported that there are still few spot goods. Therefore, fellow merchants have been actively fixing goods from overseas, with several foreign firms fixing over 60 tons, with a price of 8 taels 8 mace 5 fen in Shanghai silver. The goods are to be shipped this month, and the market is expected to be lively in the future.

The Shanghai Special City Tobacco Exchange Industry Organization Consolidation Committee has specially printed a price list to standardize the selling prices of goods of the same industry in the Chinese Concession. Yesterday, it has sent personnel to distribute the price list to various tobacco exchange stores in sections, along with an attached notice. In order to organize all industry and trade groups in the north and south markets and concessions, in order to comply with the regulations of the Industry and Commerce Union Law promulgated by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce of the National Government, which stipulates that two associations cannot be established in a single city area, under the guidance of the Business Consolidation Committee, the original Shanghai Cigarette Industry Association, the South Shanghai Tobacco Exchange Industry Association, and the North Shanghai Tobacco Exchange Industry Federation were merged and organized in order to unify and comply with the law. Therefore, on March 9th, all industry members in this city were invited to hold a general meeting to resolve to comply, and in accordance with the organizational sequence, the Shanghai Special City Tobacco Exchange Industry Organization Consolidation Committee was first established, and 15 consolidation members were elected. The second consolidation committee meeting resolved to expedite the election and actively consolidate prices in order to standardize and maintain business. Currently, in order to prevent the selling prices of goods from being confused and causing losses for the industry members, we have first set prices for several items and listed them for notification to show the standard. All industry members should comply in order to protect both principal and profit. This will not only maintain business but also promote the future of national goods. In the future, if there are price increases or decreases or if product categories and prices need to be included in this table, please inform the association at any time for contact and handling. This is hereby announced for your information.

The Drama Association declares: The association's fourteenth performance of Shakespeare's masterpiece "The Merchant of Venice" cost a huge sum of more than 3,000 yuan and consumed the efforts of dozens of people. It studies the costumes and props of 16th-century Italy and uses the latest stage equipment for the performance. All equipment is now ready in order. In addition to the original talents of the association, outstanding students from Shanghai, Jichi, Jiaoda, Patriotic and other schools were also invited to participate in the cooperation. The main actors of this drama who can be announced are: Yu Xiuyun (female) as Portia, Chen Xianmo (male) as Bassanio, Huang Yimei (male) as Antonio, and Shen Mou (male) as Shylock. By gathering talents from various school drama troupes in one place, the result of rigorous practice is that monarchs and ministers support each other, making it even more wonderful. Therefore, the re-emergence on the stage in the future will be excellent, as always expected. The association is scheduled to perform at the Central Auditorium on the nights of May 17, 18, 24, and 25. Tickets are divided into two types: one yuan and 6 jiao ocean, which are also sold separately by the Commercial Press on North Sichuan Road, the Modern Bookstore on Simalu, and the Ximen Bookstore in Laoximen.
